Consensus as Proof and the Prophet's Knowledge
The author explains why consensus is authoritative and answers the objection that the Prophet did not specify an imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why consensus (ijma') is considered an authoritative source in Islamic theology and how the Prophet's extensive knowledge of future events is used to counter objections about the imamate.

Core Idea
Consensus is authoritative because the community collectively is protected from error.

This lesson examines two interconnected arguments from classical kalam: first, the basis for the authority of consensus as a source of knowledge, grounded in the collective infallibility of the Muslim community; second, a response to the objection that the Prophet could not have specified an imam because he did not know the future. The author uses the Prophet's own statements about future events to refute this claim, showing that the imamate was known.

Guided Path
1
Understand the foundation of consensus
Read the explanation that consensus is a proof because the community as a whole is infallible, even though individuals may err.
The key term is 'isma (infallibility).
2
Grasp the analogy of collective knowledge
The author compares the community's infallibility to a single person's, using examples like intoxication from cups and satiety from morsels.
This shows that the whole has a property not found in individuals.
3
Examine the Qur'anic support
The verses 'Be with the truthful' and 'Whoever follows other than the way of the believers' are cited to show that following the community's consensus is obligatory.
4
Analyze the objection and its refutation
The objection claims the Prophet did not know the imam; the refutation lists his foreknowledge of many events, including tribulations and the Dajjal.
The Prophet's knowledge of future events is extensive.
5
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this argument supports the idea that the imam was known to the Prophet, thus countering the objection that no text exists.
The passage ends abruptly; the author continues elsewhere.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن الإجماع إنما كان حجة؛ لأن المجمعين مجموعهم معصومون عن الخطأ والكفر والضلالة، وإن كان ذلك جائزا في آحادهم فمجموع هذه الأمة في العصمة نازل منزلة شخص واحد في العصمة، ويجوز أن يثبت حكم المجموع من حيث هو جملة مجموعة، ولا يثبت لواحد منهم بخبر التواتر، فإن العلم يحصل بمجموعه وإن لم يحصل بآحاده، والسكر الحاصل من الأقداح والشبع الحاصل من اللقم وغير ذلك، وعليه حمل قوله تعالى: (يا أيها الذين آمنوا اتقوا الله وكونوا مع الصادقين) وقوله تعالى: (ويتبع غير سبيل المؤمنين).
وأما الجواب عن المعضلة التي أوردوها نقول: لا يمكن أن يقال: إن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ما كان يعرف من يجلس للإمامة بعده وينوب منابه، فإن كان يخبر أصحابه بما سيكون بعده إلى يوم القيامة من الفتن والبلايا وخروج الدجال، ولقد قال صلى الله عليه وسلم: «زويت لي الأرض فأريت مشارقها ومغاربها، وسيبلغ ملك أمتي ما زوي لي منها»، وكان يخبر أصحابه العشرة بما يفعله كل واحد ويجري عليه من القدر، وأخبر عليا رضي الله عنه: «إنك تقاتل الناكثين والقاسطين والمارقين وحديث ذي الخويصرة حيث ناظر ونافق وأنه
And know that consensus (ijma') is a proof only because the people of consensus, their totality, are infallible (ma'sumun) from error, disbelief, and misguidance. Even if that is permissible in their individuals, the totality of this community is, in infallibility, in the position of a single person in infallibility. It is permissible that the ruling of the totality is established inasmuch as it is a collective whole, and it is not established for any one of them by a mutawatir report. For knowledge is obtained by the totality even if not obtained by its individuals, like the intoxication obtained from cups and the satiety obtained from morsels and other such things. It is upon this that His statement, exalted is He, is interpreted: 'O you who have believed, fear Allah and be with the truthful' (Qur'an 9:119), and His statement: 'And whoever follows other than the way of the believers' (Qur'an 4:115). As for the answer to the difficult problem which they raised, we say: It cannot be said that the Prophet—peace be upon him—did not know who would sit for the imamate after him and deputize in his place, for he used to inform his companions of what would happen after him until the Day of Resurrection, of tribulations and calamities and the emergence of the Dajjal. He said—peace be upon him: 'The earth was folded for me, and I was shown its easts and wests, and the dominion of my community will reach what was folded for me from it.' And he used to inform his ten companions of what each one would do and what fate would befall him. And he informed 'Ali—may Allah be pleased with him: 'You will fight the breakers of the oath, the deviators, and the renegades,' and the hadith of Dhu al-Khuwaysirah when he argued and became a hypocrite, and that...
Source pages p. 492

Commentary
This passage is a twofold argument: first, an explanation of why consensus (ijma') is a valid proof in legal matters; second, an answer to an objection that the Prophet could not have known who would be the next imam. The author states that consensus is authoritative because the collective body of the community is protected from error, disbelief, and misguidance (ma'sumun), even though individuals are not infallible. The community as a whole has a special status of infallibility, analogous to a single person. The ruling of the collective is established as a whole, not by the individuals separately. Knowledge from a mutawatir report is obtained from the totality of transmitters, not from any single transmitter. The author gives analogies: intoxication from multiple cups, satiety from multiple morsels, etc. This principle is supported by Qur'anic verses: 'Be with the truthful' (9:119) and 'Whoever follows other than the way of the believers' (4:115), indicating that the community's consensus is a standard. Then the author answers a difficult problem (mu'dila) raised by objectors: the claim that the Prophet could not have known who the imam would be. The author refutes this by noting that the Prophet did inform his companions about many future events including tribulations, the Dajjal, and specific events for the ten companions and for 'Ali. The Prophet said the earth was shown to him and his community would reach those lands. Therefore, it is impossible to say he did not know the imam. The passage ends mid-sentence with the mention of Dhu al-Khuwaysirah, indicating a continuation.

Key Terms
إجماع
عصمة
مجموع
تواتر
معضلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Consensus is based on majority opinion rather than collective infallibility.
Correction: The passage clarifies that consensus is authoritative because the entire community is protected from error, not because of a simple majority.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is consensus (ijma') considered a proof?
A) Because each individual in the community is infallible.
B) Because the collective body of the community is infallible as a whole.
C) Because the Prophet explicitly designated the imam.
D) Because all Muslims agree on every issue.

Key Takeaway
Consensus is authoritative due to the collective infallibility of the Muslim community, and the Prophet's knowledge of future events shows that the imamate was known to him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to follow the Muslim community, but do you truly submit your opinions to the collective when they contradict your desires? Which part of your life are you most resistant to surrendering to the consensus of the believers?
?
The Prophet knew the future of his companions, including the trials they would face. If you knew that your own future held tests that would expose your faith, would you still dare to pray for strength—or would you rather remain ignorant?
?
Consensus protects the community from error, yet you often rely on your own reasoning. Are you willing to seek out the well-trodden path of the believers, even when your intellect finds it uncomfortable? What one step will you take today to align yourself with the truthful?

The Ambiguity of Implied Text in Consensus
The author argues that implied text in consensus is ambiguous.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why an implied text in consensus cannot decisively prove Abu Bakr's imamate due to its ambiguity.

Core Idea
Implied text is ambiguous: it may favor a specific person or the principle of consensus itself.

The author begins by addressing a key objection to the Sunni position on the imamate of Abu Bakr. Some claim that consensus implies a textual basis for his appointment. However, the author argues that such an implied text could just as well be about the authority of consensus itself, not about a specific individual. This ambiguity prevents a definitive claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation, noting the author's argument about the two possible meanings of the implied text.
Observe how the author introduces the concept of 'implied text' (النص الضمني).
2
Identify the two interpretations
The author presents two possibilities: the implied text could be about the imamate itself or about consensus being a proof. Trace each possibility in the text.
This ambiguity is central to the argument.
3
Understand the role of contextual evidence
The author mentions that contextual evidence (قرينة الحال) gave the companions certainty. Consider why this does not constitute a clear text for everyone.
The certainty of the witnesses does not amount to an explicit designation.
4
Reflect on the lesson's implication
Ask yourself: if the implied text is ambiguous, what does that mean for arguments based on consensus? This sets the stage for the next discussion on the nature of consensus.
This lesson shows the limitations of using implied texts in theological debates.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب أن النص الضمني في الإجماع ربما يكون نصا في الإمامة، وربما يكون نصا في أن الإجماع حجة، فتردد الأمرين بين هذين المحتملين، فلم يمكنا دعوى النص على أبي بكر، وذلك النص ربما لا يكون نصا ظاهرا لكن قرينة الحال عند القوم وهم شهود الحضرة ربما أورثتهم قطعا، فتنزل غير الظاهر عندهم كالظاهر، وحصل لهم القطع بذلك، واعلم أن الإجماع إنما كان حجة؛ لأن المجمعين مجموعهم معصومون عن الخطأ والكفر والضلالة، وإن كان ذلك جائزا في آحادهم فمجموع هذه الأمة في العصمة نازل منزلة شخص واحد في العصمة، ويجوز أن يثبت حكم المجموع من حيث هو جملة مجموعة، ولا يثبت لواحد منهم بخبر التواتر، فإن العلم يحصل بمجموعه وإن لم يحصل بآحاده، والسكر الحاصل من الأقداح والشبع الحاصل من اللقم وغير ذلك، وعليه حمل قوله تعالى: {يا أيها الذين آمنوا اتقوا الله وكونوا مع الصادقين} [التوبة: 119]، وقوله تعالى: {ويتبع غير سبيل المؤمنين} [النساء: 115]. وأما الجواب عن المعضلة التي أوردوها نقول: لا يمكن أن يقال: إن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ما كان يعرف من يجلس للإمامة بعده وينوب منابه، فإن كان يخبر أصحابه بما سيكون بعده إلى يوم القيامة من الفتن والبلايا وخروج الدجال، ولقد قال صلى الله عليه وسلم: «زويت لي الأرض فأريت مشارقها ومغاربها، وسيبلغ ملك أمتي ما زوي لي منها»، وكان يخبر أصحابه العشرة بما يفعله كل واحد ويجري عليه من القدر، وأخبر عليا رضي الله عنه: «إنك تقاتل الناكثين والقاسطين والمارقين» وحديث ذي الخويصرة حيث ناظر ونافق وأنه سيخرج من صيصى هذا الرجل وآيتهم ذو الثدية معروف، وما قال له في صلح الحديبية: إنك ستبتلى بمثل ما بليت به وصح ذلك يوم التحكيم، وما أطلعه الله تعالى على أمور أمته من حال أمته كما قال: {ليستخلفنهم في الأرض} [النور: 55]، وقوله: {قل للمخلفين من الأعراب ستدعون إلى قوم أولي بأس شديد} [الفتح: 16]. وما روي أنه رأى في المنام أن أبا بكر ينزع دلوا أو دلوين بضعف، وأن عمر ينزع بقوة وشدة، فقال عليه السلام: فلم أر عبقريا يفري فريه، وقال: اقتدوا بالذين من بعدي أبي بكر وعمر فيبعد كل البعد أن لا يطلعه الله تعالى على من يجلس بعده لكن لا يبعد أن لا يظهره لأحد ولا ينص على شخص؛ لأنه لم يكن مأمورا بذلك، وإن قدر أنه مأمور لزم القطع بالنص والإظهار، فإن الله تعالى بعثه هاديا مهديا وسراجا منيرا، هو الذي أرسل رسوله بالهدى ودين الحق الآية. فإن قيل: قد أظهر ذلك يوم غدير خم؛ حيث أمر الناس بالدوحات، وخاطب الناس، وأخذ بيد علي وقال: من كنت مولاه فعلي مولاه، اللهم وال من والاه وعاد من عاداه وانصر من نصره واخذل من خذله، وأدر الحق معه حيث دار، وهذا حين نزل قوله تعالى: {يا أيها الرسول بلغ ما أنزل}
And the answer is that the implied text in consensus may be a text about the imamate, and may be a text about consensus being a proof. So the matter is ambiguous between these two possibilities, so we cannot claim a clear text for Abu Bakr. And that text may not be explicit outwardly, but the contextual evidence with the people – and they were witnesses of the presence – perhaps gave them certainty, so the non-explicit became like the explicit for them, and they attained certainty thereby. Know that consensus is only a proof because the totality of those in consensus are infallible from error, disbelief, and misguidance, even if that is possible for individuals among them. So the totality of this community in infallibility occupies the status of a single person in infallibility. And it is permissible that a ruling be established for the totality by virtue of being a collected whole, and it is not established for any single individual by way of simultaneous report, for knowledge is attained by the totality even if not attained by individuals, like the intoxication resulting from cups and satiety from morsels and so forth. Upon this is understood His statement: 'O you who have believed, fear Allah and be with the truthful' [At-Tawbah 119], and His statement: 'And he who opposes the path of the believers' [An-Nisa 115]. As for the answer to the dilemma they posed, we say: It cannot be said that the Prophet, peace be upon him, did not know who would sit in the imamate after him and act as his deputy, for he informed his Companions of what would happen after him until the Day of Resurrection of tribulations, calamities, and the emergence of the Dajjal. He said: 'The earth was folded for me so I was shown its east and its west, and the dominion of my community will reach what was folded for me thereof.' He informed his ten Companions of what each one would do and what fate would befall them. He informed Ali, may Allah be pleased with him: 'You will fight the breakers of the oath, the deviators, and the renegades,' and the hadith of Dhu al-Khuwaysirah when he argued and became hypocrite, and that he would come out from the side of this man, and their sign is the one with the small breast. He told him at the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah: 'You will be tried with what I was tried with,' and that was confirmed on the day of arbitration. And Allah informed him of the affairs of his community as He said: 'He will surely grant them succession in the land' [An-Nur 55], and His statement: 'Say to those who remained behind of the Bedouins, you will be called against a people of great might' [Al-Fath 16]. And it is narrated that he saw in a dream Abu Bakr drawing a bucket or two with weakness, and Umar drawing with strength and vigor, so he said: 'I have not seen one who excels such excelling,' and he said: 'Follow the two after me: Abu Bakr and Umar.' It is far from being that Allah does not inform him of who would sit after him, but it is not far that he does not reveal it to anyone or explicitly name a person, because he was not commanded to do so. And if it is supposed that he was commanded, then the clear text and demonstration would be necessary, for Allah sent him as a guide, guided one, and an illuminating lamp—He who sent His Messenger with guidance and the religion of truth, the verse. If it is said: He did indeed demonstrate that on the day of Ghadir Khumm, when he ordered the people to the acacias, addressed them, took Ali by the hand and said: 'Whomsoever I am his master, Ali is his master. O Allah, befriend those who befriend him, and oppose those who oppose him, and support those who support him, and forsake those who forsake him, and turn the truth with him wherever he turns.' And this was when His statement descended: 'O Messenger, convey what has been revealed'
Source pages p. 492

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part argument defending the Sunni position on the imamate. It begins by addressing the claim that there is an implied text in consensus that indicates Abu Bakr's imamate. The author argues that such an implied text could equally be about the authority of consensus itself, so it is not decisive. He then explains that consensus is a proof because the community as a whole is infallible, even if individuals are not, drawing an analogy with simultaneous transmission (tawatur) where knowledge is gained from the whole not the parts. He cites Quranic verses supporting adherence to the community. Next, he responds to a dilemma: that the Prophet did not know his successor. He refutes this by listing numerous predictions the Prophet made about future events, including specific details about Ali and others, demonstrating his knowledge. He then discusses a dream about Abu Bakr and Umar and the command to follow them, concluding that the Prophet knew but may not have been commanded to announce it. Finally, he introduces an objection citing the event of Ghadir Khumm as a clear appointment of Ali. The passage ends mid-sentence with the beginning of the verse that was said to have been revealed on that occasion, leaving the objection partially answered within this window.

Key Terms
النص الضمني
الإجماع
قرينة الحال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that any indication in consensus is a clear proof for a specific imam.
Correction: The author shows that an implied text may be about the principle of consensus itself, not about a specific individual, so it cannot be used to single out Abu Bakr.

Checkpoint
What two possibilities does the author present for the implied text in consensus?
A) It is about Abu Bakr or about Umar
B) It is about the imamate or about consensus being a proof
C) It is about Ali or about the Prophet
D) It is about the Quran or about the Sunnah

Key Takeaway
An ambiguous implied text in consensus cannot serve as a decisive proof for a specific imam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter an ambiguous religious text, do you tend to favor the interpretation that supports your pre-existing beliefs, or do you honestly acknowledge the ambiguity? How can you train yourself to hold back from claiming certainty where God has not given it?
?
The companions achieved certainty through contextual evidence that you lack. Does this humble you when you think you know the truth about early Islamic history? What assumptions about the past are you holding that might be based on ambiguous rather than explicit texts?
?
If an ambiguous proof can lead to error, how carefully do you examine the foundations of your own beliefs? Are you willing to let go of a cherished opinion if it turns out to be based on an ambiguous reading?

Why Consensus is a Proof
Explanation of why consensus is a proof through collective infallibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that consensus is a proof because the collective community is infallible, analogous to simultaneous transmission (tawatur).

Core Idea
The community as a whole is infallible, even if individuals are not.

Having discussed the ambiguity of implied texts, the author now explains the true basis for consensus as a proof. He grounds it in the infallibility of the entire community, which he illustrates with a powerful analogy: just as many cups cause intoxication or many morsels cause satiety, so too does knowledge arise from the collective. He then supports this with Quranic verses.

Guided Path
1
Read the exposition on consensus
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the author's argument that consensus is a proof because the collectivity is infallible.
Pay attention to the analogy with intoxication and satiety.
2
Analyze the infallibility argument
The author says the community as a whole is like one person in infallibility. Think about how this contrasts with individual fallibility.
This is a foundational concept in Sunni theology.
3
Examine the analogy
The analogy with cups and morsels shows that knowledge can come from the totality, not from individuals. Reflect on how this relates to tawatur (simultaneous transmission).
This is a key epistemological point.
4
Connect to Quranic evidence
The author cites two verses: 'Be with the truthful' and 'Whoever opposes the path of the believers'. Consider how these support the authority of consensus.
These verses are often used in debates about communal authority.

The Prophet's Knowledge and Ghadir Khumm
Refutation of the dilemma and introduction of the Ghadir Khumm objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Prophet knew his successor but was not commanded to name him, and the objection of Ghadir Khumm is introduced.

Core Idea
The Prophet had knowledge of the future but may not have been commanded to announce the successor explicitly.

The author now tackles a dilemma: if consensus is valid, why did the Prophet not clearly name his successor? He refutes the notion that the Prophet was unaware, listing numerous prophecies. He then discusses a dream about Abu Bakr and Umar, and the command to follow them. Finally, he addresses the objection from Ghadir Khumm, which claims Ali was explicitly appointed. The passage ends mid-sentence, introducing the objection but not completing the response.

Guided Path
1
Read the response to the dilemma
Read the Arabic and translation for the refutation of the claim that the Prophet did not know his successor.
Note the many examples of prophecies listed.
2
Identify the examples of knowledge
The author gives several examples: the folding of the earth, predictions about the ten Companions, specific hadiths about Ali, and the dream about Abu Bakr and Umar. Trace each example.
These demonstrate the Prophet's comprehensive knowledge.
3
Understand the conclusion
The author concludes that the Prophet knew but was not commanded to announce. Consider the theological implication: knowledge does not necessitate public declaration.
This is a key distinction.
4
Engage with the Ghadir Khumm objection
The author presents the objection that the Prophet did appoint Ali at Ghadir Khumm. The passage ends here. Reflect on how you think the author might respond based on earlier arguments.
The answer is incomplete in this window, but the objection itself is clearly stated.

كان ذلك جائزا في آحادهم فمجموع هذه الأمة في العصمة نازل منزلة شخص واحد في العصمة، ويجوز أن يثبت حكم المجموع من حيث هو جملة مجموعة، ولا يثبت لواحد منهم بخبر التواتر، فإن العلم يحصل بمجموعه وإن لم يحصل بآحاده، والسكر الحاصل من الأقداح والشبع الحاصل من اللقم وغير ذلك، وعليه حمل قوله تعالى: {يا أيها الذين آمنوا اتقوا الله وكونوا مع الصادقين} [التوبة: 119]، وقوله تعالى: {ويتبع غير سبيل المؤمنين} [النساء: 115]. وأما الجواب عن المعضلة التي أوردوها نقول: لا يمكن أن يقال: إن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ما كان يعرف من يجلس للإمامة بعده وينوب منابه، فإن كان يخبر أصحابه بما سيكون بعده إلى يوم القيامة من الفتن والبلايا وخروج الدجال، ولقد قال صلى الله عليه وسلم: «زويت لي الأرض فأريت مشارقها ومغاربها، وسيبلغ ملك أمتي ما زوي لي منها»، وكان يخبر أصحابه العشرة بما يفعله كل واحد ويجري عليه من القدر، وأخبر عليا رضي الله عنه: «إنك تقاتل الناكثين والقاسطين والمارقين» وحديث ذي الخويصرة حيث ناظر ونافق وأنه سيخرج من صيصى هذا الرجل وآيتهم ذو الثدية معروف، وما قال له في صلح الحديبية: إنك ستبتلى بمثل ما بليت به وصح ذلك يوم التحكيم، وما أطلعه الله تعالى على أمور أمته من حال أمته كما قال: {ليستخلفنهم في الأرض} [النور: 55]، وقوله: {قل للمخلفين من الأعراب ستدعون إلى قوم أولي بأس شديد} [الفتح: 16]. وما روي أنه رأى في المنام أن أبا بكر ينزع دلوا أو دلوين بضعف، وأن عمر ينزع بقوة وشدة، فقال عليه السلام: فلم أر عبقريا يفري فريه، وقال: اقتدوا بالذين من بعدي أبي بكر وعمر فيبعد كل البعد أن لا يطلعه الله تعالى على من يجلس بعده لكن لا يبعد أن لا يظهره لأحد ولا ينص على شخص؛ لأنه لم يكن مأمورا بذلك، وإن قدر أنه مأمور لزم القطع بالنص والإظهار، فإن الله تعالى بعثه هاديا مهديا وسراجا منيرا، هو الذي أرسل رسوله بالهدى ودين الحق الآية. فإن قيل: قد أظهر ذلك يوم غدير خم؛ حيث أمر الناس بالدوحات، وخاطب الناس، وأخذ بيد علي وقال: من كنت مولاه فعلي مولاه، اللهم وال من والاه وعاد من عاداه وانصر من نصره واخذل من خذله، وأدر الحق معه حيث دار، وهذا حين نزل قوله تعالى: {يا أيها الرسول بلغ ما أنزل}
And the answer is that the implied text in consensus may be a text about the imamate, and may be a text about consensus being a proof. So the matter is ambiguous between these two possibilities, so we cannot claim a clear text for Abu Bakr. And that text may not be explicit outwardly, but the contextual evidence with the people – and they were witnesses of the presence – perhaps gave them certainty, so the non-explicit became like the explicit for them, and they attained certainty thereby. Know that consensus is only a proof because the totality of those in consensus are infallible from error, disbelief, and misguidance, even if that is possible for individuals among them. So the totality of this community in infallibility occupies the status of a single person in infallibility. And it is permissible that a ruling be established for the totality by virtue of being a collected whole, and it is not established for any single individual by way of simultaneous report, for knowledge is attained by the totality even if not attained by individuals, like the intoxication resulting from cups and satiety from morsels and so forth. Upon this is understood His statement: 'O you who have believed, fear Allah and be with the truthful' [At-Tawbah 119], and His statement: 'And he who opposes the path of the believers' [An-Nisa 115]. As for the answer to the dilemma they posed, we say: It cannot be said that the Prophet, peace be upon him, did not know who would sit in the imamate after him and act as his deputy, for he informed his Companions of what would happen after him until the Day of Resurrection of tribulations, calamities, and the emergence of the Dajjal. He said: 'The earth was folded for me so I was shown its east and its west, and the dominion of my community will reach what was folded for me thereof.' He informed his ten Companions of what each one would do and what fate would befall them. He informed Ali, may Allah be pleased with him: 'You will fight the breakers of the oath, the deviators, and the renegades,' and the hadith of Dhu al-Khuwaysirah when he argued and became hypocrite, and that he would come out from the side of this man, and their sign is the one with the small breast. He told him at the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah: 'You will be tried with what I was tried with,' and that was confirmed on the day of arbitration. And Allah informed him of the affairs of his community as He said: 'He will surely grant them succession in the land' [An-Nur 55], and His statement: 'Say to those who remained behind of the Bedouins, you will be called against a people of great might' [Al-Fath 16]. And it is narrated that he saw in a dream Abu Bakr drawing a bucket or two with weakness, and Umar drawing with strength and vigor, so he said: 'I have not seen one who excels such excelling,' and he said: 'Follow the two after me: Abu Bakr and Umar.' It is far from being that Allah does not inform him of who would sit after him, but it is not far that he does not reveal it to anyone or explicitly name a person, because he was not commanded to do so. And if it is supposed that he was commanded, then the clear text and demonstration would be necessary, for Allah sent him as a guide, guided one, and an illuminating lamp—He who sent His Messenger with guidance and the religion of truth, the verse. If it is said: He did indeed demonstrate that on the day of Ghadir Khumm, when he ordered the people to the acacias, addressed them, took Ali by the hand and said: 'Whomsoever I am his master, Ali is his master. O Allah, befriend those who befriend him, and oppose those who oppose him, and support those who support him, and forsake those who forsake him, and turn the truth with him wherever he turns.' And this was when His statement descended: 'O Messenger, convey what has been revealed'
Source pages p. 492

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part argument defending the Sunni position on the imamate. It begins by addressing the claim that there is an implied text in consensus that indicates Abu Bakr's imamate. The author argues that such an implied text could equally be about the authority of consensus itself, so it is not decisive. He then explains that consensus is a proof because the community as a whole is infallible, even if individuals are not, drawing an analogy with simultaneous transmission (tawatur) where knowledge is gained from the whole not the parts. He cites Quranic verses supporting adherence to the community. Next, he responds to a dilemma: that the Prophet did not know his successor. He refutes this by listing numerous predictions the Prophet made about future events, including specific details about Ali and others, demonstrating his knowledge. He then discusses a dream about Abu Bakr and Umar and the command to follow them, concluding that the Prophet knew but may not have been commanded to announce it. Finally, he introduces an objection citing the event of Ghadir Khumm as a clear appointment of Ali. The passage ends mid-sentence with the beginning of the verse that was said to have been revealed on that occasion, leaving the objection partially answered within this window.

العصمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some argue that because the Prophet did not explicitly name a successor, he either didn't know or didn't care.
Correction: The author shows he knew through many prophecies, but may not have been commanded to make a public declaration.

Checkpoint
What does the author list to prove that the Prophet knew who would succeed him?
A) Only one dream
B) Numerous prophecies and hadiths
C) Direct statements naming Abu Bakr
D) Consensus of scholars

Key Takeaway
The Prophet had comprehensive knowledge of his successor but was not commanded to make a public appointment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that the Prophet had knowledge of the future? How does that change the way you approach your own uncertainties in life? Will you trust his guidance more than your own plans?
?
This lesson suggests that some truths are not meant to be publicly disclosed. What area of your faith or life are you demanding certainty in, when perhaps ambiguity is the test? Can you accept not knowing who was 'right' and still live obediently?
?
If the Prophet, with all his knowledge, did not explicitly name a successor, are you willing to admit that your preferred interpretation might be based on inference rather than a clear command? What does that mean for your allegiance to that interpretation?

Prophet's Knowledge of Caliphs and Non-Obligation of Explicit Naming
Author presents evidence for Prophet's knowledge of future caliphs and argues he was not commanded to name them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Prophet Muhammad was aware of the future caliphs through divine revelation and dreams, but he was not commanded to explicitly name them, and why this does not necessitate public designation.

Core Idea
Knowledge does not necessitate public declaration; the Prophet knew but was not commanded to name.

In this passage, the author uses several prophetic hadiths and Quranic verses to demonstrate that the Prophet was informed of future events concerning the Muslim community, including the caliphs. However, he argues that having this knowledge does not imply that the Prophet was obligated to explicitly name the caliphs. The key distinction is between being aware of something and being commanded to disclose it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the many examples the author gives to show the Prophet's knowledge.
2
Identify the evidence for the Prophet's knowledge
List the different hadiths and Quranic verses mentioned. Understand how each demonstrates the Prophet's awareness of future events, including the caliphs.
The examples include the emergence of the Khawarij, the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah, the promise of succession, and the dream about Abu Bakr and Umar.
3
Understand the argument about non-obligation
The author concludes that it is unlikely Allah would not inform the Prophet, but it is possible the Prophet did not reveal it. Why? Because he was not commanded to do so. Consider the implications.
If he had been commanded, he would have made a definitive designation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سيخرج من صيصى هذا الرجل وآيتهم ذو الثدية معروف، وما قال له في صلح الحديبية : إنك ستبتلى بمثل ما بليت به وصح ذلك يوم التحكيم، وما أطلعه الله تعالى على أمور أمه من حال أمته كما قال : ( ليستخلفنهم في الأرض [النور: ٥٥]، وقوله : ( قل للمخلفين من الأعراب ستدعون إلى قوم أولي بأس شديد [الفتح : ١٦]. كان وما روي أنه رأى في المنام أن أبا بكر ينزع دلوا أو دلوين بضعف، وأن عمر ينزع بقوة وشدة، فقال عليه السلام فلم أر عبقريا يفري فريه، وقال: اقتدوا بالذين من بعدي أبي بكر وعمر فيبعد كل البعد أن لا يطلعه الله تعالى على من يجلس بعده لكن لا يبعد أن لا يظهره لأحد ولا ينص على شخص؛ لأنه لم يكن مأمورًا بذلك، وإن قدر أنه مأمور لزم القطع بالنص والإظهار، فإن الله تعالى بعثه هاديًا مهديًا وسراجًا منيرا هو الذي أرسل رسوله بالهدى ودين الحق الآية.
There will emerge from the descendants of this man, and their sign is the one with the breast like a breast, known. And what He said to him in the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah: 'You will be tested with something similar to what you were tested with, and that was verified on the day of Tahkeem.' And what Allah Almighty informed him of the affairs of his community from the situation of his community, as He said: {He will surely make them successors in the land} [al-Nur 24:55], and His saying: {Say to those who remained behind of the Bedouins, 'You will be called to a people of severe might'} [al-Fath 48:16]. There was also what was narrated that he saw in a dream that Abu Bakr was drawing a bucket or two buckets with weakness, and that Umar was drawing with strength and severity, so he (peace be upon him) said: 'I have never seen a genius doing his work like that,' and he said: 'Follow those after me, Abu Bakr and Umar.' Then it is extremely far that Allah Almighty would not inform him of who would sit after him, but it is not far that he would not reveal it to anyone and not explicitly name a person; because he was not commanded to do so. And if it is assumed that he was commanded, then definitive designation and manifestation would be necessary. For Allah Almighty sent him as a guide, rightly guided, and a shining lamp, He who sent His Messenger with guidance and the religion of truth, the verse.
Source pages p. 493

Commentary
This passage is a proof argument. The author first lists several hadiths that demonstrate the Prophet's knowledge of future events concerning the Muslim community: the emergence of the Khawarij (the man with the breast), the test at Hudaybiyyah, the promise of succession, and the dream about Abu Bakr and Umar drawing water. These show that the Prophet was informed of many details. Then the author argues that it is extremely unlikely that Allah would not inform him of who would succeed him as caliph. However, it is possible that the Prophet did not reveal that knowledge to anyone nor explicitly name a person, because he was not commanded to do so. If he had been commanded, he would have had to make a definitive designation and public declaration. The passage concludes by affirming that Allah sent the Prophet as a guide and a light, and that he delivered the message.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that if the Prophet knew the caliphs, he must have explicitly named them, and the lack of naming proves he did not know.
Correction: The author clarifies that knowledge does not necessitate public declaration. The Prophet was not commanded to name them, so his silence does not negate his knowledge.

Checkpoint
What does the author conclude from the hadiths about the Prophet's knowledge?
A) The Prophet was commanded to name the caliphs.
B) The Prophet knew the caliphs but was not commanded to name them.
C) The Prophet did not know the caliphs.
D) The Prophet named Abu Bakr explicitly.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet was aware of the future caliphs through divine revelation and dreams, but he was not commanded to explicitly name them; thus, his silence on specific names does not undermine his knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Prophet was not commanded to name the caliphs, why do you feel the need to insist on something he did not do? What does your insistence reveal about your own need for certainty?
?
The Prophet knew but remained silent. In your own life, when you know something that would be divisive, are you willing to follow his example and remain silent out of obedience? Or do you feel compelled to speak even when not commanded?
?
Consider the dream of Abu Bakr and Umar. The Prophet saw their strengths and weaknesses and still did not name them as caliphs. How does this challenge your assumption that knowledge must be acted upon? What knowledge do you have that you have not acted upon, and why?

Ghadeer Khum and Counter-Evidence for Abu Bakr
Objection from Ghadeer Khum and response with counter-hadiths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sunni scholars respond to the Ghadeer Khum argument by citing comparable hadiths in favor of Abu Bakr's caliphate.

Core Idea
The Ghadeer Khum hadith is not exclusive; similar evidence exists for Abu Bakr.

In this passage, the author anticipates a major Shia argument based on the event of Ghadeer Khum. After presenting the objection with its supporting hadiths, he offers a robust reply: if such reports are accepted as evidence, then one must also accept the abundant reports that point to Abu Bakr as the rightful caliph. This lesson examines both sides of the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the first part of the passage (the Ghadeer Khum argument) and note the key hadiths cited: the 'master' hadith, Umar's congratulation, the station of Aaron, and the city of knowledge.
Notice how the objector uses multiple hadiths to support the claim of caliphate for Ali.
2
Identify the author's response
Find the shift starting with 'قيل: إن اقتنعتم...' where the author introduces counter-evidence for Abu Bakr.
The author does not deny the Ghadeer hadith but instead offers parallel hadiths.
3
List the counter-hadiths
Identify each hadith cited for Abu Bakr: the request for writing materials, leading prayer, the description of the four caliphs, the Quraysh hadith, and the Abbas inquiry.
These are all from Sahih Muslim.
4
Reflect on the argumentative strategy
Consider why the author presents these hadiths. He is showing that similar evidence exists for Abu Bakr, thus undermining the exclusivity of the Ghadeer argument.
This is a common Sunni refutation strategy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: قد أظهر ذلك يوم غدير خم؛ حيث أمر الناس بالدوحات، وخاطب الناس، وأخذ بيد علي وقال: من كنت مولاه فعلي مولاه، اللهم وال من والاه وعاد من عاداه وانصر من نصره واخذل من خذله، وأدر الحق معه حيث دار، وهذا حين نزل قوله تعالى: { يا أيها الرسول بلغ ما أنزل إليك من ربك وإن لم تفعل فما بلغت رسالته } [المائدة: ٦٧]، وقد فهم الجماعة من قوله: «من كنت مولاه فعلي مولاه» الخلافة؛ حيث هنأه عمر فقال: بخ بخ يا علي أصبحت مولى كل مؤمن ومؤمنة، وقال عليه السلام: أنت مني بمنزلة هارون من موسى إلا أنه لا نبي بعدي، وقد قال عليه السلام: أنا مدينة العلم وعلي بابها إلى غير ذلك من الأخبار. قيل: إن اقتنعتم بمثل هذه الأخبار فخذوا منا في حق أبي بكر كذلك، روى مسلم في صحيحه أنه قال عليه السلام: ائتوني بدواة وكتف أكتب لأبي بكر كتابا لا يختلف عليه اثنان، وقال: ليصل بالناس أبو بكر، وقال: إن وليتموها أبا بكر تجدوه ضعيفا في نفسه قويا في أمر الله تعالى، وإن وليتموها عمر تجدوه قويا في نفسه قويا في أمر الله، وإن تولوها عثمان يسلك بكم مسلك السداد، وإن تولوها عليا تجدوه هاديا مهديا يأخذ بكم الطريق المستقيم، وقال: لا يزال هذا الأمر في قريش ما بقي منهم اثنان. وقال حملة الحديث لما نزلت سورة الفتح جاء العباس إلى علي رضي الله عنهما وقال: إني أعرف الميت في وجوه بني عبد المطلب، وأنى برسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وقد نعى إليه، فانطلق بنا إليه نسأله لمن الأمر بعده، فإن كان فيكم
If it is said: He made that manifest on the day of Ghadeer Khum, when he ordered the people to [gather under] the trees, and addressed the people, and took Ali's hand and said: 'Whoever I am his master, Ali is his master. O Allah, befriend whoever befriends him and oppose whoever opposes him, and support whoever supports him and abandon whoever abandons him, and turn the truth with him wherever he turns.' And this was when the saying of Allah Almighty was revealed: {O Messenger, convey what has been revealed to you from your Lord, and if you do not, then you have not conveyed His message} [al-Ma'idah 5:67]. And the group understood from his saying 'Whoever I am his master, Ali is his master' the caliphate; for Umar congratulated him saying: 'Congratulations, congratulations, O Ali, you have become the master of every believing man and woman.' And he (peace be upon him) said: 'You are to me as Aaron was to Moses, except that there is no prophet after me.' And he (peace be upon him) said: 'I am the city of knowledge and Ali is its gate.' And other such reports. It is said: If you are convinced by such reports, then take from us similar reports in favor of Abu Bakr. Muslim narrated in his Sahih that he (peace be upon him) said: 'Bring me an inkpot and a shoulder bone, I will write for Abu Bakr a document after which two will not dispute.' And he said: 'Let Abu Bakr lead the people in prayer.' And he said: 'If you entrust it to Abu Bakr, you will find him weak in himself, strong in the matter of Allah; if you entrust it to Umar, you will find him strong in himself, strong in the matter of Allah; if you entrust it to Uthman, he will tread with you the path of rectitude; if you entrust it to Ali, you will find him a guide, rightly guided, taking you on the straight path.' And he said: 'This matter will remain among Quraysh as long as two of them remain.' And the bearers of hadith said: When Surah al-Fath was revealed, al-Abbas came to Ali (may Allah be pleased with them both) and said: 'I recognize death in the faces of Banu Abd al-Muttalib, and I sense that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) has been informed of his death. So let us go to him and ask him: For whom is the matter after him? For if it is among you...'
Source pages p. 493

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector raises the Ghadeer Khum event, citing the hadith 'Whoever I am his master, Ali is his master' and the accompanying supplication, and claims that the companions understood it as a designation of caliphate, as shown by Umar's congratulation. Additional hadiths are cited: the station of Aaron, and the city of knowledge. The author's response is that if one accepts such reports as evidence, then one must also accept similar reports in favor of Abu Bakr. The author then lists several hadiths from Sahih Muslim: the request for writing materials for Abu Bakr, the hadith about leading prayer, the hadith describing the qualities of the four caliphs, the hadith about Quraysh, and the incident with al-Abbas asking about succession. The author implies that these reports provide equally strong evidence for Abu Bakr's caliphate, thus refuting the exclusivity of the Ghadeer argument.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Ghadeer Khum hadith alone proves Ali's exclusive right to caliphate.
Correction: The author argues that similar hadiths exist for Abu Bakr, showing that the evidence is not exclusive.

Checkpoint
How does the author respond to the Ghadeer Khum argument?
A) He denies the authenticity of the hadith.
B) He provides similar hadiths in favor of Abu Bakr.
C) He argues that the hadith is misinterpreted.
D) He accepts the hadith but says it does not imply caliphate.

Key Takeaway
Sunni scholars argue that the Ghadeer Khum hadith does not exclusively support Ali's caliphate, as similar evidence exists for Abu Bakr.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a hadith like Ghadeer Khum, do you immediately accept the interpretation that favors your own sect? How would you feel if you discovered you had been ignoring equally strong evidence for the other side? Would you be willing to change your stance?
?
The objector in this passage selected only hadiths that support Ali. Are you guilty of selective evidence in your own beliefs about early Islamic history? What would it take for you to honestly examine the counter-evidence? Make a firm intention today to seek truth wherever it leads.
?
If you were present at the Prophet's deathbed, would you have prioritized documenting his succession as the companions did? Or would you have been content with what you already believed? What does your answer reveal about your attachment to your own opinions over the Prophet's explicit instructions? Repent from stubbornness and ask Allah for guidance.

Hadith Evidence for Election of the Imam
Author enumerates hadiths for both sides and concludes for election.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a set of hadiths is woven into a cumulative argument for the principle that the caliphate is determined by election (ikhtiyar) rather than explicit designation (nass).

Core Idea
The hadith as a totality support election, not a single designated text.

This passage captures a pivotal point in Islamic political theology: Was the caliphate established by a clear text (nass) designating Ali, or by the community's choice (ikhtiyar)? The author presents a series of hadiths that, when read together, point unmistakably to election. He first cites the so-called Shia proof texts (like 'Man kuntu mawlahu') but then counters with equally strong reports about Abu Bakr, and closes with a narrative that underscores the Prophet's openness on the matter.

Guided Path
1
Read the whole passage once
Read the Arabic passage and its translation without pausing to analyse. Let the argument unfold naturally from the Prophet's words to the author's conclusion.
2
Identify the two groups of hadiths
The passage first lists hadiths that are often used to support Ali's claim (the 'city of knowledge', 'man kuntu mawlahu', etc.). Then it cites reports about Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman that are equally compelling for election.
Notice how the author frames the second group as a reply to Shia reasoning.
3
Examine the story of al-Abbas
The anecdote about al-Abbas asking the Prophet about succession, and the Prophet's sermon in response, shows that no explicit name was given. Instead, the Prophet gave general advice about leadership and care for his family.
This story directly refutes the idea of a clear text.
4
Understand the conclusion
Read the final sentence: 'وَهٰذَا كُلُّهُ مِنَ الْأَخْبَارِ دَلِيلٌ عَلَى الِاخْتِيَارِ.' The author explicitly states that all these reports together are evidence for election, not for nass.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إليك من ربك وإن لم تفعل فما بلغت رسالته، وقد فهم الجماعة من قوله: «من كنت مولاه فعلي مولاه» الخلافة؛ حيث هنأه عمر فقال: بخ بخ يا علي أصبحت مولى كل مؤمن ومؤمنة، وقال عليه السلام: أنت مني بمنزلة هارون من موسى إلا أنه لا نبي بعدي، وقد قال عليه السلام: أنا مدينة العلم وعلي بابها إلى غير ذلك من الأخبار. قيل: إن اقتنعتم لمثل هذه الأخبار فخذوا منا في حق أبي بكر كذلك، روى مسلم في صحيحه أنه قال عليه السلام: ائتوني بدواة وكتف أكتب لأبي بكر كتابا لا يختلف عليه اثنان، وقال: ليصل بالناس أبو بكر، وقال: إن وليتموها أبا بكر تجدوه ضعيفا في نفسه قويا في أمر الله تعالى، وإن وليتموها عمر تجدوه قويا في نفسه قويا في أمر الله، وإن تولوها عثمان يسلك بكم مسلك السداد، وإن تولوها عليا تجدوه هاديا مهديا يأخذ بكم الطريق المستقيم، وقال: لا يزال هذا الأمر في قريش ما بقي منهم اثنان. وقال حملة الحديث لما نزلت سورة الفتح جاء العباس إلى علي رضي الله عنهما وقال: إني أعرف الميت في وجوه بني عبد المطلب، وأنى برسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وقد نعى إليه، فانطلق بنا إليه نسأله لمن الأمر بعده، فإن كان فيكم فأنتم وذاك، وإن كان في غيركم أوصى بكم إلى الوالي، فأبى عليه علي ورجع العباس إلى النبي فقال له في ذلك، فخطب الخطبة المعروفة إلى قوله: إلا من ولي هذا الأمر فليقبل من محسنهم وليتجاوز عن مسيئهم، فقيل: يا رسول الله، أوص بقريش، فقال: الناس تبع لقريش، ثم قال: أوصيكم بأهل بيتي وعترتي خيرا؛ فإنهم لحمي، احفظوا منهم ما يحفظون فيما بينكم، وهذا كله من الأخبار دليل على الاختيار.
To you from your Lord, and if you do not, then you have not conveyed His message. And the group understood from his saying: 'Whoever I am his master, Ali is his master' the caliphate; when Umar congratulated him saying: 'Well done, O Ali, you have become the master of every believing man and believing woman.' And he, peace be upon him, said: 'You are to me like Aaron to Moses, except that there is no prophet after me.' And he, peace be upon him, said: 'I am the city of knowledge and Ali is its gate,' and other such reports. It was said: If you are convinced by such reports, then accept from us similarly regarding Abu Bakr. Muslim narrated in his Sahih that he, peace be upon him, said: 'Bring me an inkwell and a shoulder blade, I will write for Abu Bakr a book after which two will not disagree.' And he said: 'Let Abu Bakr lead the people in prayer.' And he said: 'If you entrust it to Abu Bakr, you will find him weak in himself but strong in the command of God Almighty; if you entrust it to Umar, you will find him strong in himself and strong in the command of God; if you entrust it to Uthman, he will lead you on the path of rectitude; if you entrust it to Ali, you will find him a guide and guided, taking you on the straight path.' And he said: 'This matter will remain among Quraysh as long as two of them remain.' And the bearers of hadith said: When Surah al-Fath was revealed, al-Abbas came to Ali, may God be pleased with them both, and said: 'I recognize death in the faces of the sons of Abd al-Muttalib, and I see the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, has been informed of his death. Let us go to him and ask him for whom the authority is after him. If it is among you, then you are that; if it is among others, let him entrust you to the ruler.' So Ali refused, and al-Abbas returned to the Prophet and spoke to him about that. Then he delivered the well-known sermon up to his saying: 'Except that whoever undertakes this authority, let him accept from their good-doer and overlook their wrongdoer.' And it was said: 'O Messenger of God, advise us concerning Quraysh.' He said: 'The people are followers of Quraysh.' Then he said: 'I advise you to treat my household and my kin well; for they are my flesh. Preserve from them what they preserve among you.' And all of these reports are evidence for election.
Source pages p. 494

Commentary
This passage is a cumulative argument from hadiths to prove that the caliphate is determined by election (ikhtiyar) rather than explicit designation (nass). The author begins by citing the well-known hadith 'Whoever I am his master, Ali is his master' and notes that the Companions understood from it the caliphate, as seen in Umar's congratulation. Additional hadiths about Ali's status are mentioned. The author then anticipates a counterargument: if one accepts these reports for Ali, one must also accept similar reports for Abu Bakr, provided by Muslim. These include the Prophet's intention to write a document for Abu Bakr, his command for Abu Bakr to lead prayer, and his descriptions of the four caliphs' qualities. Another narration recounts the incident when al-Abbas asked the Prophet about succession, and the Prophet responded with a sermon emphasizing justice and care for his family. The author concludes that all these narrations together support the principle of election, implying that no explicit text designates a specific individual.

Key Terms
اختيار
النص
الإمام
الخلافة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the hadith 'Man kuntu mawlahu' alone proves explicit designation of Ali as caliph.
Correction: The author shows that even if one accepts that hadith, there are equally strong reports for Abu Bakr, and the overall evidence points to election.

Checkpoint
What conclusion does the author draw from the hadiths presented?
A) The caliphate is based on explicit designation (nass).
B) The caliphate is based on election (ikhtiyar).
C) The caliphate is reserved for Quraysh only.
D) The caliphate must be determined by ijtihad.

Key Takeaway
The cumulative weight of these hadiths demonstrates that the caliphate was meant to be decided by the community's choice, not by a single explicit text.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet intended to write a document for Abu Bakr to prevent disagreement, yet he refrained. When you face a decision in your community or family, do you trust the collective process enough to let go of your own insistence on a specific outcome? What is one area where you need to surrender control to communal wisdom?
?
The author shows that both sides (Ali and Abu Bakr) have hadiths that could be used to claim designation. Yet the cumulative argument supports election. Is there a deeply held belief you cling to because of a single piece of evidence, while ignoring the broader picture? Will you honestly examine that belief today?
?
In the sermon, the Prophet said 'accept from their good-doer and overlook their wrongdoer.' Who in your life have you been unwilling to overlook or accept because they did not meet your standards? How does this hadith challenge your heart to change that attitude this week?

Objection: The Imam Must Be Designated Explicitly
An objection argues the Imam must be known through nass, not election.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the kalam objection that imamate requires explicit divine designation (nass) rather than human election (ikhtiyar), and the reasoning why the Imam's essential attributes cannot be known through conjecture.

Core Idea
The Imam’s essential attributes can only be known through revelation, not human reasoning.

This passage presents a forceful objection from those who argue that the Imam must be appointed directly by the Prophet through divine revelation. The objector claims that the Imam possesses unique attributes—such as infallibility, perfect knowledge, courage, and justice—that cannot be reliably assessed through ordinary human judgment (ijtihad) or outward appearances. Only explicit designation from God, conveyed through the Prophet, can guarantee that the Imam truly possesses these qualities. Read carefully to see the logical structure of this objection, which sets the stage for a response later in the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim
Read the first sentence: 'طريق العلم بتعيين الإمام النص دون الاختيار'. That is the core claim. Note how the objector frames it as the only way.
The word 'النص' means explicit designation, often a direct statement from the Prophet.
2
List the required attributes
The objector lists the attributes the Imam must have: عصمة (infallibility), علم وعقل (knowledge and intellect), شجاعة (courage), عدل على الرعية (justice towards subjects). Understand each.
These are high-level qualities that are difficult to verify.
3
Understand the epistemological argument
The objector argues that these attributes cannot be known through ijtihad or conjecture (غلبات الظنون). Only nass based on revelation can establish them. Grasp this epistemological claim.
This is a key point: certain truths require divine guarantee.
4
Consider the practical danger
The objector warns that without nass, electing Imams based on outward appearances risks having heretics (زنادقة) in secret, leading to corruption of religion and law. Reflect on this consequence.
This strengthens the objection by showing the harmful results of the opposing view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: إنما قلنا: طريق العلم بتعيين الإمام النص دون الاختيار؛ لأن الإمام يجب أن يكون على صفات مخصوصة؛ منها العصمة، ومنها العلم والعقل، ومنها الشجاعة، ومنها العدل على الرعية، ولا مجال للاجتهاد وغلبات الظنون في معرفتها ومعرفة مقاديرها، بل لا يعلم ذلك إلا بالنص من الرسول مستندا إلى وحي من الله، فإذا كنتم تختارون الأئمة بظواهرهم وتجوزون أن يكونوا من الزنادقة في الباطن، وأن يكذبوا على الله ورسوله وأن يعطلوا الحدود ويبطلوا الحقوق، ويتأولوا متشابهات القرآن على غير وجهها وينقلوا الأخبار على
For it is said: We only say that the way of knowing the appointment of the Imam is explicit designation (nass), not election (ikhtiyar); because the Imam must possess specific attributes: among them infallibility, knowledge and intellect, courage, and justice towards the subjects, and there is no room for ijtihad and dominant conjectures in knowing them and knowing their measures; rather, that is known only through explicit designation from the Messenger, based on revelation from God. Since you elect the Imams based on their outward appearances and consider it permissible that they be heretics in secret, and that they lie about God and His Messenger, and suspend the prescribed punishments and invalidate rights, and interpret ambiguous Quranic passages in other than their proper way, and transmit reports in a [corrupt] manner...
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage presents an objection against the position of election (ikhtiyar). The objector states flatly that the only valid method for designating an Imam is explicit designation (nass) from the Prophet, not election. The reason is that the Imam must have specific essential attributes: infallibility (isma), knowledge and intellect, courage, and justice towards the subjects. These attributes cannot be reliably known through ijtihad (independent reasoning) or mere probable conjectures; only divine revelation via the Prophet can establish them. The objector then warns of the practical danger of election: if Imams are chosen based on outward appearances, it is possible that they are inwardly heretics (zanadiqa) who would lie about God and His Messenger, neglect the prescribed punishments, invalidate people's rights, misinterpret ambiguous Quranic verses, and corrupt the transmission of hadith. The objection thus challenges the supporters of election to explain how they can guarantee the presence of these essential attributes without divine designation.

Key Terms
النص
الاختيار
عصمة
اجتهاد
زنادقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the objection, what is the only way to know the Imam's essential attributes?
A) Through ijtihad and consensus of the scholars.
B) Through explicit designation (nass) from the Prophet based on revelation.
C) Through election by the community.
D) Through the Imam's own claim.

Key Takeaway
The objection argues that because the Imam's essential attributes cannot be known through human judgment, only explicit divine designation suffices.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a leader you admire in your community—whether a scholar, an activist, or a family elder. On what basis do you trust them? Is it their outward piety, eloquent speech, or reputation? The objector argues that outward appearances can conceal inner corruption. Have you ever been deceived by someone's external image? What would it take for you to be absolutely certain that a leader is truly guided by God, not just skilled at presenting themselves?
?
The objector claims that only explicit designation from the Prophet can guarantee the Imam's attributes. If you were to choose between two leaders—one claiming divine appointment through clear textual evidence and one selected by popular vote—which would you follow? This is not a hypothetical puzzle; it is a decision that shapes your religious loyalty. What criteria do you actually use to decide whom to follow, and are those criteria grounded in revelation or in your own preferences?
?
Consider the attributes the objector lists: infallibility, knowledge, courage, and justice. Honestly, do you know anyone in your life who possesses all these perfectly? How certain are you of that? The objection forces you to confront the limits of human judgment. Are you willing to demand a higher standard of certitude for your spiritual guides, even if it means questioning deeply held assumptions?

Objection against election of the imam and its refutation
The author presents an objection against election and refutes it by arguing that imamate attributes are inferable from signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that only nass can appoint the imam, and the Sunni response that the required attributes can be inferred from observable signs.

Core Idea
Imamate qualities can be inferred from signs, not solely from divine designation.

In this passage, the author presents a key objection from those who argue that the imam must be appointed by explicit textual designation (nass) because of the required attributes like infallibility and knowledge. The author then refutes this by showing that these attributes can be known through observable signs (amarat), drawing an analogy to how we assess witnesses and judges.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note that it begins with evidence for election, then an objection, then a refutation.
Pay attention to the dialectical structure: evidence → objection → refutation.
2
Identify the opponent's argument
The opponent claims that only nass can determine the imam because the required attributes (isma, knowledge, courage, justice) cannot be known by ijtihad or conjecture. Find these points in the text.
The opponent also warns about the risk of appointing hypocrites, citing Umayyad conduct.
3
Analyze the author's refutation
The author responds that the attributes can be inferred from signs (amarat): words indicate knowledge, good actions indicate chastity, skill in war indicates policy and courage. This is analogous to assessing qualifications for testimony or judgeship.
The author adds that if corruption appears later, the imam can be removed.
4
Reflect on the Umayyad example
Why does the opponent bring up the Umayyads? How does the author handle this? Notice that the author acknowledges the reports but says they do not negate imamate according to those who permit such conduct in imams.
This reveals a key sectarian difference about the permissibility of sin in imams.
5
Summarize the lesson
Write one sentence summarizing the main argument of the passage. Then check your understanding with the checkpoint.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأنتم وذاك، وإن كان في غيركم أوصى بكم إلى الوالي، فأبى عليه علي ورجع العباس إلى النبي فقال له في ذلك، فخطب الخطبة المعروفة إلى قوله: «إلا من ولي هذا الأمر فليقبل من محسنهم وليتجاوز عن مسيئهم»، فقيل: يا رسول الله، أوص بقريش، فقال: «الناس تبع لقريش»، ثم قال: «أوصيكم بأهل بيتي وعترتي خيراً؛ فإنهم لحمي، احفظوا منهم ما يحفظون فيما بينكم»، وهذا كله من الأخبار دليل على الاختيار.

فإن قيل: إنما قلنا: طريق العلم بتعيين الإمام النص دون الاختيار؛ لأن الإمام يجب أن يكون على صفات مخصوصة؛ منها العصمة، ومنها العلم والعقل، ومنها الشجاعة، ومنها العدل على الرعية، ولا مجال للاجتهاد وغلبات الظنون في معرفتها ومعرفة مقاديرها، بل لا يعلم ذلك إلا بالنص من الرسول مستندا إلى وحي من الله، فإذا كنتم تختارون الأئمة بظواهرهم وتجوزون أن يكونوا من الزنادقة في الباطن، وأن يكذبوا على الله ورسوله وأن يعطلوا الحدود ويبطلوا الحقوق، ويتأولوا متشابهات القرآن على غير وجهها وينقلوا الأخبار على غير طريقها افتراء على الله ورسوله، أولم يعهد من بني أمية التعرض لأهل البيت قتلا وهتكا للحرمة واستحلال للأموال؟ أولم ينقل عنهم الظلم والجور على الرعايا وملابسة الفسق والفجور؟ فما يؤمنكم أن متابعتكم أئمة الجور تورثكم النار وبئس المصير؟

قيل: صفات الإمامة يجوز أن يستدل عليها بالأمارات، والأقوال تدل على العلم والفضل، وحسن الأفعال تدل على العفة، والمهارة بالحرب تدل على السياسة والشجاعة، فكما يستدل بالأفعال على الشهادة والقضاء كذلك يستدل على الصفات التي تشترط في الأئمة، وإن ظهر بعد ذلك جهل أو جور أو ضلال أو كفر انخلع منها أو خلعناه، وما ينقل عن الأموية فهو صحيح إلا أنه لا ينافي الإمامة عندهم وعند من يجوز ذلك على الأئمة.
You and that [story], and if [the succession] were in someone else, he [the Prophet?] would have entrusted you to the governor, but Ali refused him, and al-Abbas returned to the Prophet and spoke to him about that, and he delivered the well-known sermon up to his saying: 'Only whoever takes charge of this matter should accept good from their good-doer and overlook their wrongdoer.' It was said: O Messenger of God, advise concerning Quraysh. He said: 'The people are followers of Quraysh.' Then he said: 'I advise you good regarding my household and my family; for they are my flesh and blood. Preserve from them what they preserve among you.' All of these reports are evidence for election (al-ikhtiyar).

If it is said: We only say that the way of knowledge for appointing the imam is textual designation (al-nass), not election (al-ikhtiyar); because the imam must possess specific attributes: among them infallibility (al-isma), knowledge and reason, courage, and justice towards the subjects. There is no room for ijtihad and dominant conjectures in knowing them and knowing their measures. Rather, that is only known through textual designation (al-nass) from the Messenger, based on revelation from God. So if you elect imams based on their outward appearances and allow that they might be hypocrites (zanadiqa) inwardly, and that they might lie against God and His Messenger, and suspend the prescribed penalties (hudud) and invalidate rights, and interpret the ambiguous verses of the Quran in other than their proper manner, and transmit reports in other than their proper way, fabricating against God and His Messenger – has not the conduct of the Umayyads been witnessed: attacking the Prophet's household (Ahl al-Bayt) by killing and violating sanctity and legalizing wealth? Has not their injustice and tyranny towards subjects and their involvement in immorality and lewdness been reported? What gives you assurance that your following of oppressive imams will not earn you the Fire? What an evil destination!

It is said: The attributes of imamate (al-imama) may be inferred from signs (al-amarat). Words indicate knowledge and virtue; good actions indicate chastity; skill in war indicates policy and courage. Just as actions are used to infer [qualifications for] testimony and judgeship, so too they are used to infer the attributes required in imams. If after that ignorance, injustice, deviance, or unbelief appears, he is removed from it or we remove him. What is reported about the Umayyads is true, except that it does not contradict imamate according to them and according to those who permit that in imams.
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical unit: first, the author asserts that the narrated reports about the Prophet's advice regarding Ahl al-Bayt and Quraysh serve as evidence for the validity of election (al-ikhtiyar) as a method for appointing the imam. Then an opponent objects, arguing that the only way to know the rightful imam is through explicit textual designation (al-nass) from the Prophet, because the imam must possess specific attributes: infallibility (al-isma), knowledge and reason, courage, and justice towards the subjects. The opponent claims that these qualities cannot be determined by ijtihad or conjecture; only nass based on revelation can assure them. The opponent further argues that election based on outward appearances risks appointing hypocrites who would corrupt religion and law, and points to the historical conduct of the Umayyads as evidence of such risk. The author responds that the qualities required for imamate can be inferred from observable signs: words (speech and statements) indicate knowledge and virtue; good actions indicate chastity; skill in war indicates political acumen and courage. This is analogous to how one infers qualifications for testimony or judgeship from actions. If after appointment the imam displays ignorance, injustice, deviance, or unbelief, he may be removed from office. As for the reports about the Umayyads, the author acknowledges their truth but argues that they do not negate the legitimacy of their imamate according to those who hold that such actions do not necessarily disqualify an imam.

Key Terms
نص (nass)
اختيار (ikhtiyar)
عصمة (isma)
إمامة (imama)
أمارات (amarat)
اجتهاد (ijtihad)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the qualities of imamate can only be known by divine revelation, and that election is invalid because it relies on conjecture.
Correction: The author shows that the qualities can be inferred from observable signs (amarat) such as words and actions, just as we assess witnesses and judges. Therefore election (ikhtiyar) is a valid method.

Checkpoint
According to the author's refutation, how can the qualities required for imamate be known?
A) Only through explicit textual designation (nass) from the Prophet
B) Through independent reasoning (ijtihad) and conjecture
C) Through observable signs (amarat) such as words and actions
D) Through the consensus of the community

Key Takeaway
The imam's required qualities can be inferred from observable signs (amarat) like words and actions, and if corruption appears, he can be removed.

Conditions of Allegiance: Number of Witnesses
Author enumerates opinions on witnesses for allegiance and poses a question on caliphal removal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the differing scholarly opinions on the number of witnesses required for the contract of allegiance (bayʿah) and the legal implications of a caliph's removal.

Core Idea
Allegiance is validated by scholarly consensus, not crowd size.

The proper procedure for establishing a caliph was a matter of debate. In this passage, the author reports multiple opinions on how many witnesses are needed for the oath of allegiance. He also raises a related question: if a caliph resigns or commits wrongdoing, does removal happen automatically or only after a ruling? This sets the stage for understanding the role of ijtihād in political theology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the numbers mentioned
Read the passage and note the different numbers of witnesses proposed by scholars: one just man, two men, four men, or a group of qualified decision-makers.
These are all valid opinions in the tradition.
2
Understand the sufficiency condition
Notice that if one person contracts the allegiance and no one objects, it is sufficient – but witnesses are still required due to the gravity of the matter.
3
Ponder the question on removal
The author asks whether a caliph who resigns or commits acts that merit removal is automatically removed or merely deserves removal. He says this is a matter of ijtihād.
This question shows the practical implications of the discussion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم من زاد والعدد لعقد البيعة، فقيل : تتم البيعة برجل عدل، وقيل: برجلين، وقيل بأربعة وقيل بجماعة من أهل الحل والعقد والاجتهاد والبصيرة بالأمور، ولو عقد واحد ولم يسمع من الباقين نكير كفى ذلك، ويجب الإشهاد به فإنه خطب جسيم ومنصب عظيم، والمسائل المرتبة على ما ذكرناه من عقد البيعة لرجلين في صقعين أو إقليمين فإنه إذا خلع نفسه أو أحدث أحداثا يستحق بها الخلع ، أينخلع أم يستوجب ذلك كله من مظان الاجتهاد؟ وليراجع الكتب المصنفة في الكلام فإني لم أشترط على نفسي في هذا الكتاب نقل ما ذكر في الكلام، وإنما شرطت حل المشكلات من المعقولات وبيان منتهى إقدام أهل الأصول في مراتب العقول دون المنقول.
And among them are those who added the number for the contract of allegiance. It was said: allegiance is completed by one just man, and it was said: by two men, and it was said: by four, and it was said: by a group of those who loosen and bind, who are mujtahids and insightful in affairs. And if one person contracts it and no objection is heard from the rest, that suffices. And it is necessary to have witnesses for it, for it is a grave matter and a great office. The questions that arise from what we have mentioned about the contract of allegiance for two men in two regions or two provinces: if he removes himself or commits acts that merit removal, is he removed or does he deserve that? All of that is a matter of ijtihad. And one should refer to the books composed on kalam, for I have not stipulated for myself in this book to transmit what has been mentioned in kalam, but rather I have stipulated to solve the problems of rational matters and to explain the utmost limits of the steps of the people of fundamentals in the levels of intellects, not transmitted matters.
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage addresses two distinct but related topics: the conditions for the contract of allegiance (bayʿah) and the author's methodological restrictions. First, the author presents differing opinions on the number of witnesses required for a valid bayʿah. Some say one just man, others two, others four, and still others a group of qualified decision-makers (ahl al-ḥall wa-l-ʿaqd). He then notes that if a single person performs the contract and no one objects, it is sufficient, though witnesses are still required due to the gravity of the matter. He then raises a further question: if the caliph resigns or commits actions that warrant removal, is he automatically removed or does he merely deserve removal? This, he says, is a matter of ijtihād. Finally, the author clarifies his own approach in this book: he does not intend to transmit all the transmitted reports (manqūl) discussed in kalam works, but rather to focus on solving problems of rational theology (maʿqūlāt) and to explain the furthest limits of reasoning attained by the masters of uṣūl.

Key Terms
بيعة
أهل الحل والعقد
اجتهاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the number of witnesses for allegiance is fixed and uniform across all scholars.
Correction: The passage shows multiple valid opinions (one, two, four, or a group), and even allows a single contract without objection to be sufficient, indicating flexibility.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is required if only one person performs the contract of allegiance?
A) It is invalid.
B) It is sufficient if no objection is heard, but witnesses are still necessary.
C) It requires at least four witnesses.
D) It is only valid if a group of qualified people approve.

Key Takeaway
The number of witnesses for allegiance is not rigidly fixed, and the question of caliphal removal is a matter of ijtihād.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own life, do you trust that a leader appointed by a small group of qualified people is legitimate, even if you didn't witness the process? What does this say about your reliance on scholarly authority?
?
The passage treats the caliph's removal as a matter of ijtihad, not a fixed rule. Are you willing to accept that some issues in Islam are open to scholarly reasoning, even when they involve leadership? How does that affect your certainty about religious rulings?
?
If you were in a position to accept or reject a leader, would you demand a public pledge from many witnesses, or would you be satisfied with the approval of a few knowledgeable people? What does your preference reveal about your priorities: communal consensus or trust in expertise?

Sects and Disagreements
beginner
4 min
Author's Methodological Focus: Reason Over Tradition
Author states his methodological focus on rational theology over transmitted reports.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author restricts his work to rational theology (maʿqūlāt) and excludes transmitted reports (manqūl).

Core Idea
This book solves rational problems, not transmitted ones.

After discussing political theology, the author clarifies his own method. He directs readers to other works for transmitted traditions, explaining that his goal is to solve the most challenging rational theological problems and to show the ultimate reach of human intellect. This distinction is crucial for understanding the scope of his work.

Guided Path
1
Identify what the author excludes
The author says he has not stipulated to transmit what is mentioned in kalam (i.e., transmitted reports). He directs readers to other books for that.
This is a methodological boundary.
2
Identify what the author includes
He has stipulated to solve the problems of rational matters (maʿqūlāt) and to explain the ultimate limits of the steps of the people of fundamentals in the levels of intellects.
This is his self-imposed task.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Consider why a theologian would choose to focus on rational theology over transmitted reports. What advantage does this approach offer?
Think about clarity and universality of reason.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم من زاد والعدد لعقد البيعة، فقيل : تتم البيعة برجل عدل، وقيل: برجلين، وقيل بأربعة وقيل بجماعة من أهل الحل والعقد والاجتهاد والبصيرة بالأمور، ولو عقد واحد ولم يسمع من الباقين نكير كفى ذلك، ويجب الإشهاد به فإنه خطب جسيم ومنصب عظيم، والمسائل المرتبة على ما ذكرناه من عقد البيعة لرجلين في صقعين أو إقليمين فإنه إذا خلع نفسه أو أحدث أحداثا يستحق بها الخلع ، أينخلع أم يستوجب ذلك كله من مظان الاجتهاد؟ وليراجع الكتب المصنفة في الكلام فإني لم أشترط على نفسي في هذا الكتاب نقل ما ذكر في الكلام، وإنما شرطت حل المشكلات من المعقولات وبيان منتهى إقدام أهل الأصول في مراتب العقول دون المنقول.

Key Terms
معقولات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the author is rejecting transmitted knowledge altogether.
Correction: He is not rejecting it; he is merely delimiting the scope of this particular book to rational theology, and he refers readers to other works for transmitted reports.

Checkpoint
What does the author state about the scope of his book?
A) He will transmit all discussions found in kalam books.
B) He will solve rational problems and explain the limits of intellect, not transmitted matters.
C) He will focus only on transmitted reports.
D) He will ignore both rational and transmitted matters.

Key Takeaway
The author's book is dedicated to rational theology (maʿqūlāt), not to transmitting traditional reports (manqūl).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a theological question, do you instinctively seek a transmitted text or do you engage with rational proofs? Where does your comfort lie, and what might that reveal about your approach to faith? Will you challenge yourself to explore the 'ma'qūlāt' side more deeply?
?
The author says he is solving 'the problems of rational matters.' Think of a personal doubt or question you have never been able to answer. Have you truly wrestled with it rationally, or have you avoided it by relying on easy transmitted answers? What would it cost you to honestly engage with that problem?
?
This book is for those who seek the 'utmost limits of the steps of the people of fundamentals.' Are you willing to push your intellect to its limits, even if it means leaving behind the safety of familiar transmitted reports? What is one step you can take today to begin that journey?
